===== PAGE 5 =====
The Jewish Theological Seminary
Jewish Museum
Only superlatives can describe the program of the Jewish Theological Seminary of
America. The faculty consists of some of the greatest scholars in the world. The Library
houses the largest Jewish manuscript collection and Jewish rare book collection in the
world. The Teachers’ Institute and Seminary school have made a most vital contribution
to the entire field of Jewish education. The Jewish Museum, the largest collection of
Jewish ceremonial objects in the world, gives anyone who enters its portals a feeling of
pride in the artistic creativity of our people down through the generations.
Eternal Light programs and schools of religion have publicized the program of the
Seminary throughout the United States. But members of the
Conservative Movement are the last to realize our great depend¬
ence on the program of the Seminary. From the education
of our Rabbi to the curriculum of our religious schools, from
the program of our United Synagogue Youth to the content of
our Adult Education Institute, we could not begin to act with¬
out the help of the Seminary. It is our mother organization,
and our synagogue and congregation gains its strength and de¬
velopment as it receives more and more nourishment from the
central organization of the entire Conservative Movement. As
our mother upholds us in time of need, so must we be conscious
of our need for her constant guidance.
Ritual and
In keeping with the theme of our Year Book, the synagogue cannot be at the hub
of a community without performing its primary function, that of ritual and worship.
Our congregation has indeed extended itself to give to its membership meaningful and
inspiring services. From the High Holidays to the Friday evening and Sabbath morning
services a major effort has been made to keep our services both traditionally beautiful
and decorously inspiring. To this end we must express our appreciation to our entire
membership for their cooperation in making these services the object of admiration on
the part of visitors from all parts of the United States.
Our staff too deserves an expression of appreciation for their constant assistance espe¬
cially in the reading of the Tor,ah. In this regard we want to pay a special thanks to
Mr. Joel Bressler for the many times he has read the Torah at both our Sabbath and
Holiday services as well as at our daily worship services.
Religious worship is indeed unique, for the realization of its goals is not dependent
so much on the flawless efforts of those officiating as it does on the personal and sin¬
cere efforts of the worshippers themselves. We ,all create the moment and that moment
is felt more deeply when we experience it together. May we realize the importance of
the opportunity to worship together, for each other, for ourselves, for all Israel, for all
mankind.
Nathan Friedlin
Chairman
45

Boy Scout Troop 14
Scoutmaster Dr. Harry Yergin
Asst. S coat masters Allie Goldstein, Milton Hecht and William Rose
Chairman of Scout Committee Norman Moss
Institutional Representative Ted Freedman
Committee Members: Bob Fischer
Bernie Moskovitz
Robert Weiss
Morris Doueck
Shelby Trager
Nathan Weiss
)oe Mizrahi
Joe P. Safer
DR. HARRY YERGIN
Scoutmaster
Another banner year in the annals of Scouting for Troop 14
started this past year with a swim and hot dog party at the home
of Mr. and Mrs. Joe Wilensky, with several new boys joining
the Troop and bringing our total membership to 44 active
Scouts. The next long hike took place with the three day Ross
Allen annual Camporee in October at Silver Springs, Fla. Our
entire troop came home with an excellent rating in this under¬
taking. Other excursions throughout the year were visits to
the U.S.S. Roosevelt Aircraft Carrier, a three day hike to Camp
Echokotee, another three day hike to Keystone Heights on Lake
Brooklyn and our big summer Scouting activity, the summer
Scout Camp where 21 of our Scouts enjoyed the outdoors for
an entire two week period. While at camp Jordan Harris, Joe
Saportas and Leon Talpalar were tapped and initiated into the
Order of the Arrow, an honorary society for Scouts.
The Flying Eagle Patrol won the annual contest based on
attendance, advancement and patrol participation. The Patrol
was led by Eagle Scout Leon Yergin and consists of Randy Sil-

Young Judaea
Jerry Linsey
Pres. District II
Eve Aptheker
Tova
Rose Zager
Zionettes
Benjie Felder Gilda Goldman
Hashomerim Bas Yisroel
Club Leaders
Hashomerim Mrs. Melvin Wise, Dr. Arthur Burns
Zionettes Marilyn Hal pern, Asst.
Bas Yisroel Sybil Horovitz, Margy Sapor tas
Tova Elaine Brukner, Judy Bossen
Highlighting senior activities was the District Conclave held
in March. Mrs. William Goldman was adult chairman and Miss
Elaine Brukner was conclave chairman.
The culminating affair of the year for junior and senior clubs
was the Israeli Fair held on the grounds of the River Garden
Home in May with the proceeds going to the Israeli Scouts.
Eleven Judeans attended the Southern Region Summer Con¬
vention at Camp Judaea in Hendersonville, N. Car. in June.
The following were elected to serve as officers: Jerry Linsey,
District II Pres.; Michael Pousman, Regional Treasurer; Mal¬
colm Fages, Regional Programming Committee.
Camp Judaea in Hendersonville is a major project of Young
Judaea. Hadassah and Z.O.A. sponsor this 4 or 8 week camp
period with a full camping and Zionist program. Camp Judaea
serves to develop in youth the ideals of American freedom, an
appreciation of the Jewish people, a bond with the land of
Israel and an understanding of the religious and ethical con¬
cepts of Judaism.
760 RIVERSIDE

Rosh Hodesh Adar
30 SHEVAT
Rosh Hodesh Adar
1 ADAR
2 ADAR 3 ADAR
4 ADAR
HAMISHA ASAR B’SHEVAT (Fifteenth Day of Shevat), the
New Year of the Trees. Often referred to as the Jewish
Arbor Day, this holiday commemorates the ancient need for
trees in the Holy Land. It is celebrated everywhere with appropriate songs
and games. Fruits long associated with the trees that once grew in the
Holy Land (and have begun to grow there again) are eaten on this day,
as part of the celebration. In Israel, the day is also observed in a very
practical way. There, where the land had been denuded by centuries of
neglect, and the need for trees has re-arisen (and reforestation has be¬
come a national goal), children and adults plant trees throughout the
land.

A new era has begun! The youth of America are taking
a great part in making the world a better place in which to
live. At least this is true of the youth of Aleph Zadik Aleph.
This year has been devoted to bringing about an awareness
of the fact that it is up to us to strive toward such goals as
a fuller Jewish education, the abolishment of racial and re¬
ligious intolerance and world peace. No longer can there be

LOUISE HILSENRAD
B’nai B’rith Girls, junior order of B’nai B’rith Women,
climaxed a tremendously successful year. Among our many ac¬
tivities, B.B.G. ,along with our brother Alephs sponsored a
North Llorida Council Workshop and an Inter-Laith Service.
Some of the highlights of the year in B.B.G. were a "Roaring
Twenties" dance, several bake sales, a trip to Hope Haven Hos¬
pital, a salami sale, a candy sale, a contribution to the Interna¬
tional Service Lund, and an end-of-the-year party.
To conclude this year an annual Installation Luncheon was
held. A plaque for the "Most Outstanding Girl" was presented
to Lesley Kidder by the Past President of B’nai B’rith Women,
Mrs. Jack Dorman.

EMANUEL EHRLICH
B’nai B’rith promotes a platform of brotherhood, fellowship
and interfaith amity. B’nai B’rith works tirelessly on behalf of
many worthy community projects.
A. B. Weil Lodge #800, B’nai B’rith will strive under its
new officers to build up its membership and achieve a goal for
the betterment of this community. Interesting luncheon meetings
are held at the Hotel George Washington the second and fourth
Thursdays of every month, with four dinner meetings during
the year. The annual Scholarship Fund Dance will be held on
November 17 to provide funds for scholarship loans to worthy
Jewish boys and girls to further their education.
The men of B’nai B’rith are united to make its program play
a vital role in the future of our community.
Bhai B rith Women
President Mrs. Martin Brown
Vice-Presidents Mrs. Abe Stein, Mrs. Norman Danglo,

B’nai B’rith Women subscribe to the principle that to secure
the future we must deeply serve others before we can serve
ourselves. The Jacksonville chapter has made tremendous prog¬
ress in upholding the motto of all B’nai B’rith women: Service,
Fidelity and Devotion, by supporting various national B’nai
B’rith philanthrophies such as National Jewish Hospital, Leo
N. Levi Hospital, Bellfaire Children’s Home and support to
Israel projects.
Board of B’nai B’rith Women
Among our local services include help to Pinecastle School,
River Garden Home, the blind, the Anti-Defamation League
which distributed memo calendar books to the public schools
and "Dolls for Democracy” program. The B’nai B’rith Women
sponsor and give guidance to our youth groups, A.Z.A. and
B.B.G.

■■■ ■■ - - —-
SHIV’AH ASAR B’TAMMUZ (17th Day of Tammuz), a fast day
followed by 3 weeks of mourning. It commemorates the breach¬
ing of the walls of Jerusalem by the Babylonians, which led
to the exile of the Jews. (Our symbol, the catapult.)
TISHA B’AB (9th Day of AB), anniversary of the destruction
of the 1st and 2nd Temples—a fast day climaxing a 9-day
period of mourning.

IS YOUR CHILD GETTING THE MOST OUT OF SUMMER?
Not unless he is developing the cooperative spirit, say psycholo¬
gists. Not unless he is getting fresh air and proper exercise
continually, say physicians. Not unless he is gaining confidence
learning new skills—atheletic, dramatic and manual—say edu¬
cators.
All agree—the aswer is summer camp . . . you can’t afford not
to send your child!
CAMP OCALA is Florida’s finest summer camp for Jewish
boys and girls, ages 5 - 16. Your child develops into maturity
faster here . . . having fun all the time . . . under guidance of
qualified counselors—1 to every 2t/2 youngsters (3 times the
national average). It is located in the cool hills and lakes of
Ocala National Forest in north central Florida. For free de¬
scriptive brochure write—Camp Ocala — 1431 N. Bayshore
Drive—Miami, Florida.

===== PAGE 49 =====
The newest addition to our already outstanding synagogue
program is the creation of our Foundation School. We have
completed one year with our first grade and the results have
been fruitful and gratifying. Our first graders are adept both
in English and Hebrew and their progress in relation to the
general school curriculum has been excellent.
Dr. and Mrs. Jack Rosner served as the chairmen of the
Parents’ Committee; Mr. Jack Becker did a yeoman task in
raising the funds to make our school possible; Mrs. Marsha
Berdit was in charge of transportation. The cooperation of all
parents was indeed of the finest.
Mrs. Sheldon Gendzier will be the chairman of the P.T.A.
this year with Mrs. Louis Safer as Secretary and Mrs. Robert
Wolf as Treasurer. The room mothers for the first grade are
Mrs. Edward Bernard and Mrs. Irving Hacker. For second
grade the room mothers are Mrs. Raymond Cohen and Mrs.
Jack Shorstein. Mrs. Frank Rosenberg and Mrs. Morton Ben¬
jamin will serve as Chairman and Co-Chairman of the fund
raising committee. Program coordinator will be Mrs. Moshe
V. Goldblum.
Mrs. Marilyn Sandler and Mrs. Jewell Varnedo have been
engaged to teach this year and will be assisted by Mrs. Leon
Zucker.

===== PAGE 52 =====
Songs for the Home
KINDLING OF THE SABBATH LIGHTS
The Sabbath is welcomed into the Jewish
home by the mother kindling the Sabbath
candles. She shields her eyes from the
light so that with the completion of the
blessing she sees the light for the first
time in all its Sabbath warmth and
splendor.
KIDDUSH (Santificaron)
The father of the household makes the
family deeply conscious of the sanctity of
the Sabbath through the recitation of the
Kiddush over the cup of wine.
SHOLOM ALEICHEM (Peace unto You)
The Sabbath meal should be spent in the
singing of Sabbath melodies and we in¬
clude the Sholom Aleichem, for it is the
beautiful hymn by which we welcome the
angels of peace who bring us the Sab¬
bath. Only the first two verses are chant¬
ed by the Cantor.
BIRHAT HAMAZON (Grace After Meals)
At the conclusion of the meal the family
is asked to thank God for all of the
blessings of food, home, family and its
love. The prayer of indebtedness is called
the Birchat Hamazon or Grace After
Meals. The Cantor chants the first para¬
graph of the Birchat Hamazon.
BIRHOT HATORAH
(Blessing over the Torah)
On Sabbath morning in the synagogue
we are often called to the Torah. The
democracy of Judaism is clearly expressed
for at the most solemn moment in the
service, the reading of the Torah, all are
considered worthy of coming forward to
offer their personal blessing.
YOM ZE L’YISROEL
N’RAN’NA
Two Hebrew Melodies emphasizing the
uniqueness of the Sabbath and our unique
obligation of reacting with both reverence
and happiness.
This Book is Dedicated
To Our Many Loyal Advertisers
Who H ave Made the Year Book Possible.

Activities
Kindergarten Purim Play Presented in the Auditorium
Our New Sunday Afternoon Program
90 boys and 30 girls took part in our Sunday Afternoon Program which consisted of social ballroom dancing instruction with
Maria Douglas studios, Gymn athletics consisting of volleyball, Jai Alai, basketball and badminton, while the boys took part in a
six-team intramural baseball league.
Our six team baseball league was coached by Ed Witten, Chuck Slott, Jerry Cohn, Fred Shenkman, Ivan Tobias and Benjie Felder.
A year round program of football, basketball and baseball is planned for the coming year, under the supervision of Robert
Fischer.

HANUKAH (Dedication) — Anniversary of the day when the
Jews, led by Judah Maccabee and his brothers, freed the
Temple from Syrian invaders. At the Tample’s rededication,
only enough undefiled oil was found to light the Holy Lamp for one day„
Miraculously, if burned eight days. Thus, on the first day of Hanukah,
Jews light one candle of the Menorah (eight-branched candlestick, our
symbol), adding another flame each day until all eight are lit.

A second year of this relatively new social club for younger
married couples ended successfully. Several outstanding month¬
ly affairs have been held under the advisorship of the Vice-
President Richard Jafa, with a different Board member in charge
of each monthly affair working together with their wives.
Our organization is open to all married couples through
the age of 32. For membership please contact the Treasurer
Lawrence Jaffe.

River Garden Hebrew Home for the Aged
President Joe Becker
Executive Vice-President &
....Chairman Admissions Samuel J. Thier
Vice-President & Co-
Chairman Admissions Arthur j. Gutman
Vice-President & Co.
Chairman Admissions Martin Lind
Vice-President & Chairman
House Committee Albert Kofka
Vice-President & Chairman Public Relations Gus Bonnett
Vice-President & Chairman
Residents Welfare Mrs. A. Horovitz
Vice-President & Medical Director Dr. Harry Reinstme
Secretary Frank Diamond
Treasurer Donald Cohn
Chairman Board of
Trustees & Hon. President Irving Klepper
The River Garden story is a continuing one since 1946. It
is a story of elderly people who find comfort and security when
their way of life is disrupted in the community. There are many
reasons for coming to the Home, but all too often physical
changes and infirmities associated with the later years makes it
difficult for the aged to live alone or with their families.
The broad gamut of medical and nursing service provides
basic security for the residents of the Home. However, enrich¬
ing and adding meaning to the lives of elderly people is equally
as important as the basic services required for daily living. To¬
wards these goals, the Home has organized a wide range of so¬
cial, religious, educational, crafts, and work activities to broaden
the horizon of most of the Home-bound residents. With the
help of the corps of Gray Ladies, personal relationships are
maintained and group programs are planned to provide the
motivation to find living worth while.
To meet the increasing demands for its services, River Gar¬
den is planning 'to open the door for 50 more.” This slogan
implies a large building program to increase the capacity from
70 to 120 residents. The near future will see the fruition of
these plans translated into brick and mortar.
It is with pride that River Garden views its past 16 years of
service to the Jewish Communities of Florida and looks forward
to continuing to provide a dignified ,and secure way of life for
many more of our aged.
Best Wishes For a Happy & Healthy New Year
Mr. & Mrs. HARRY BEGAL

This year the Esquire Club has had a very successful year.
We wish to thank our sweetheart, Bonnie Barnert, and our
Advisor, Byron Selber, for their efforts on our behalf.
The outstanding social events were the Annual Holiday
Dance at the Robert Meyer Hotel and the Esquire Week-end
at Atlantic Beach.
The service projects included contributions to the Center
and participation in the annual Cerebral Palsy Telethon.
Jewish War Veterans
Lt. Meyer Leibovitz Post #199
Jewish War Veterans of U.S.A.
The J. W. V. is an organization of Veterans of all wars
with Posts through-out the entire United States. It was orga¬
nized in 1896 and chartered by the United States Congress in
the same year being the oldest veteran organization in America,
with its headquarters in Washington, D. C.
All war veterans are invited and urged to .affiliate with
J. W. V. and participate in its activities.

United Synagogue Youth
CENTER YOUTH LEAGUE
Center Youth League Officers. First row, left to right:
Jerry Safer, Treas.; Jack Fleet (Regional Office); Karen
Gaslar, Corres. Secretary; Linda Halpern, Rec. Secretary;
Eddie Mizrahi, President. Second row, left to right: Bruce
Yergin (Regional Office); Bruce Gibbs, Vice-Pres.; Rich¬
ard Kidder, Vice-Pres.; Marvin Slott, Vice-Pres.
Another banner year was enjoyed by our oldest USY
group, as we had over 20 attend the Regional Convention
in Miami Beach while five delegates represented us ,at the
National Convention in New York. Religious, social, cul¬
tural and athletic activities are just a part of our well-
rounded program.
Fred Shenkman and Susan Edwards were the recipients
of our Best Boy and Girl awards at our annual Banquet
held each May.
Center Youth League Board
CHARLES PALOT CLUB BOYS
Front row, left to right: Jack Mizrahi, Vice-President;
Harold Sutton, Recording Secretary; Howard Rosenblatt,
Corres. Secretary; Leonard Selber, Vice-Pres. Second row:
Chuck Slott, Vice-President; Leon Yergin, Treas.; Jerry
Portnoy, President; Robert Fischer, Director.
For the first time our CPC Club was split to allow more
members to participate and separate boys and girls chapters
were formed, with both clubs looking forward to banner
years with the boys and girls competing with each other.
Charles Palot Club Boys Board
CHARLES PALOT CLUB GIRLS
Front row, left to right: Madelyn Levin, Board Mem¬
ber; Sheila Pages, Vice-President; Phyllis Glossman, Cor¬
res. Secretary; Anita Mesnick, Vice-Pres.; Sheila Kramer,
President. Second row: Gail Price, Board Member; Debby
Lederman, Treasurer; Sharon Weiss, Recording Secy.; Judy
Horovitz, Vice-Pres.
A major activity for our USY chapters is the Leadership
Training Institute which is held during the month of
August with a full ten day experience of Jewish living in
the outdoors. 33 of our members from the 3 USY chapters
attended the 1962 LTI held at Camp Blue Star in Hender¬
sonville, N. Car. This is the largest delegation the Jackson¬
ville chapters have ever had ,and surpasses all other syna¬
gogues in the S. E. Region.
Charles Palot Club Girls Board
Advisors for the coming year are: CYL—Mrs. Ann Lewis and Stanley Kantor; CPC Boys
—Pepi Spielberger and Enid Goldberg; CPC Girls—Evelyn Brauner and Arlene Gamce.

Progressive Credit Union
President Moe B. Safer
Vice-President Israel Lipson
Secretary Eugene L. Henry
Treasurer Joseph Cohen
Directors Max Rubin, Benjamin Fink, Louis
Berinhout, Edwin Presser
Assoc. Directors S.amuel Schuster, M. B. Glickstein,
Herman Gelman, Sanford M. Whitman,
and Leo Jacobson
Credit Committee Samuel J. Klepper, Chairman; Louis
Moss and Harry Kline
Supervisory Committee Isidore Weiss, Chariman; Max
Becker, Herbert Sandler
OFFICERS
The Progressive Credit Union sponsored by the Jewish
Progressive Society and chartered by the State of Florida, has
continued to grow in its 23 years. The combined membership
of Credit Unions in the U.S. totals more than 14 million mem¬
bers and has over four billion dollars in assets.
From a very modest beginning of 20 members and $500.00
in assets, the Progressive Credit Union has grown to over 350
members and almost ]/4 million in assets. It is organized to
encourage thrift and provide a safe, convenient medium whereby
members can invest and accumulate savings. Being regularly
examined by the Comptroller of the State, the savings of mem¬
bers are safeguarded in several ways.
The Progressive Credit Union carries life savings insurance
and loan protection insurance with the Cuna Mutual Insurance
Society for the benefit of its members. The premiums for this
coverage are paid for by the Credit Union without any cost to
the individual members. Last year the Board declared a 3%
dividend on savings and 10% rebate of interest to borrowing
members.
The year’s activities climax with the annual dinner meeting
at the Center. A cordial invitation is extended to anyone who
wishes to join.

Girl Scouts and Brownies
MRS. LEON SCHINASI
Chairman Mrs. Leon Schinasi
Brownie Troop #210. Leader Mrs. Jack Joffre
Co-Leader Mrs. Joseph Kowitz
Brownie Troop #28, Leader Mrs. Leo Moskovitz
Co-Leader Mrs. Herbert Feinberg
Brownie Troop #269, Leader Mrs. Harold Newman
Co-Leaders Mrs. I. P. Edwards
Mrs. Stanley Trussel
Mrs. Bernard Marón
Girl Scout Troop #6, Leader Mrs. Irvine Kowitz
Co-Leader Mrs. Seymour Steiner
Girl Scout Troop #193, Leader Mrs. Harold Gershman
L
Co-Leaders Mrs. Selwyn Savage
and Mrs. Robert Gulden
The Brownie and Girl Scout Troops sponsored by the
Center Sisterhood have again shown how our youth group ac¬
tivities are growing through the Center. Looking back through
the years we find some of our leaders today were our Girl
Scouts of yesteryears.
We have two active Girl Scout Troops, one in the Arlington
area and one in the Southside area. Our Brownies have one
Troop in Arlington and two in Southside.
This year Girl Scouts celebrated their 50th anniversary. In
this period the organization started with 12 girls in Savannah,
Ga. Today three and a half million girls and adults in all
fifty states and in foreign countries belong to Girl Scouts of
the U.S.A. This shows Scouting holds something for girls
through the generations.
This coming year we look forward to continuing our pro¬
gram with the help of our mothers who give their time and
efforts to those girls who are eager to learn just what Scouting
is.
3 of our Troops are pictured on this page.

TAANIT ESTHER (Fast of Esther)—This holiday commemorates
the heroism of Esther, beautiful Jewish Queen of Persia.
Joined by her people, she fasted for three days before risking
her life by appearing unsummoned before her King Ahasuerus. Her
pleas led to the salvation of the Jewish people and the downfall of
Haman (see Purim, below).
PURIM (literally, “lots”)—this gayest of Jewish holidays is
nonetheless named for the lots cast before Haman to select
a day of execution for the Jews. On the fateful day, how¬
ever, it was the wicked Haman who perished—thanks to Queen Esther
and her cousin, Mordecai. The full story is told in the Megillah (Book
of Esther, our symbol) which, on this day, is read aloud twice in the
synagogue. During the reading, children twirl their gragers (noise-
makers) whenever Haman is mentioned, to drown out his name.

Presiden ts Message
PRESIDENT’S MESSAGE
As vve approach the New Year, each of us must
honestly concede that the Jacksonville Jewish Center
plays an important role in our respective lives. For
our own welfare, therefore, each of us should do
everything in our power to make our institution the
finest Synagogue Center possible. This means not
only giving the Center maximum financial support
so that vital activities may continue, but also taking
an interest in the program and devoting personal
time and energy to assure successful carrying out of
the program. This can be done by serving on one of
our many committees, by becoming active in our
Sisterhood and Men’s Club, by teaching in our school
system, by enrolling in our adult education program,
by attending daily and Sabbath services, to mention
just a few possibilities.
This will prove beneficial not only to the Center
but also to you as a member, because persons who
participate personally in our program are more un¬
derstanding of our goals and acquire a greater sense
of dedication to the preservation of Jewish ideals and
tradition.
I am confident that you will receive much satis¬
faction out of your participation. Also, when you
realize that the Jacksonville Jewish Center offers the
finest program of any synagogue center in the south¬
east, your affiliation will be more greatly valued by
you. The success of our fine program requires the
support of all of our members. Please make a pledge
now to do your part this coming year in being an
active, participating member of the congregation.
Your help is needed and will be appreciated.
May we work together toward achieving the goal
of our High Holiday prayer:
“May all Thy children unite in one fellowship,
To do Thy will with all their heart.’’
Le Shonah I or ah Tikatevu.
The Southeast Region of the United Synagogue Convention in Miami Beach. Our
delegates seated around the table at the Banquet: Jack Becker, Mrs. Moshe V. Goldblum,
Rabbi Goldblum, Louis Safer, Dr. Nathan Schneider, David I. Weinstein, Nathan
Freidlin.

Ladies Hebrew Sheltering A id Society
OFFICERS
President Mrs. Moe B. Safer
Vice-President Mrs. William Goldman
Vice-President Mrs. Roy J. Sloat
Recording Secretary Mrs. William Silverman
Financial Secretary Mrs. Ben Fink
Corresponding Secretary Mrs. Sam Lazarus
Treasurer, Dues Mrs. I. Zaslow
Treasurer, Projects Mrs. Louis Witten
Ladies Hebrew Sheltering Aid Society was founded 39 years
ago as an aid society to help the needy of the Jewish faith. It
was always the dream and hope of our founders to have a
Home for the Aged in Jacksonville. This dream became a
reality when River Garden Hebrew Home for the Aged was
founded. Since that time, our role became that of the auxiliary
to the Home.
We provide extra-budgetary needs such as furnishings,
redecorating, air conditioning, kitchen and infirmary equipment.
Funds for these needs were raised through Tombola, Donor
and Social Printing projects as well as annual dues and life
memberships in Ladies Aid. Linens were provided by our an¬
nual Linen Shower.
We sponsor a Grey Ladies Program, regularly scheduled
entertainment and parties. River Garden residents participate
OFFICERS
in projects served by the auxiliary such as the residents’ maga¬
zine, Ceramic classes and the Hobby Shop.
The Golden Sunshine Club of River Garden which emerged
from our weekly Senior Citizens meetings has grown into a
self-sufficient organization giving fellowship and companion¬
ship as well as participating in civic and philanthropic activities.
This year Ladies Aid pledges to continue its efforts and
cooperation in bringing not only the material but the spiritual
values that our elder citizens hold so dear.

MRS. LOUIS SLOTT
To understand the importance of Sisterhood women, we
must be able to visualize the place of Sisterhood in the entire
communal pattern. The Sisterhood is organized primarily to
help the Synagogue. As an auxiliary of the Synagogue its func¬
tion is to promote Jewish educational, religious and social activ¬
ity among the wives of Synagogue members as well as their
friends and mothers of the children who attend its religious
schools.
Many thanks to the members of the Sisterhood executive
board, to the chairmen of the various committees and to the
many women who gave of their time and their talents to make
the past year so successful in every phase of Sisterhood activity.
Thanks also to the members of the entire congregation and
their friends who so loyally supported our fund-raising affairs,
for without you it would have been difficult to achieve our
many goals.
Our plans for the future are great, but we need YOU!
We can pool our efforts and together create or achieve some¬
thing richer and finer than what anyone of us can do alone.
The best wishes of the Jacksonville Jewish Center Sister¬
hood are extended to you and your dear ones for a happy and
healthy New Year.
Sisterhood Officers at Closing Luncheon Meeting

Center Year Book
1962-63
5723
¡heme of the Year Book
Galicia Synagogue
A Timber synagogue, 17th century. This is a typical
small town synagogue in Eastern Europe.
%
For the past 2500 years the synagogue has served as the
focal point of all Jewiish community life. Even when the
Temple in Jerusalem still stood, it was the synagogue that
served the community in each local area.
To this very day the synagogue serves the three-fold pur¬
pose of Jewish life, as a place of worship, of study and social
gathering. The pictures and drawings of the many synagogue
edifices of the American Jewish community show the wonder¬
ful facilities that congregations everywhere are providing for
their membership.
As the synagogue has preserved Jewish life down through
the generations, so must it continue to preserve Judaism today.
It can only do so if we permit it to be a part of our personal
and communal lives.
The cover of our Year Book portrays some of the beautiful
synagogues of our land that are serving as centers of their
communities. In moving counter clockwise, we see the beau¬
tiful edifices of Milburn, N. J., the Temple in Cleveland, Ohio,
the New York City Central Synagogue, B’nai Amoona in St.
Louis, Mo. and Chizuk Amuno in Baltimore, Md.
The Synagogue is the very "tree of life" of American Jewry.
It was there to deeply imbed its roots in the rock soil of Ameri¬
can culture and it is here today to help in the flowering of
Jewish life in our own midst.
Akron, Ohio — Synagogue Beth El
3

PRE-USY CLUB
Left to right: Jason Solomon, Religious Ch.; Elaine Lin-
sey, Recording Secretary; Bobby Norman, Treasurer; Eileen
Feinberg, Corr. Secretary; Hilda Goldman, President; Ricky
Speizer, 2nd Vice-Pres.; Gilda Goldman, 1st Vice-Pres.;
Elliott Baker, Sergeant-at-Arms.
Our newest USY group consists of 8th grade boys and
girls who meet bi-weekly with emphasis being placed on
Pre-USY orientation. Their activities will be geared to
prepare them for membership in our older USY chapters.
Ada Hinda Block and Linda Gartner will be their advisors
for 1962-63.
PRE-USY CLUB OFFICERS
MAJOR S PRE-TEENS
Officers pictured at left for the coming year are Jackie
Bettman, Secretary; Susan Gendzier, Treasurer; Debbie
Morris, President; Davida Weiss, 2nd Vice-Pres.; Irving
Weinstein, 1st Vice- Pres.
The 7th grade boys and girls enjoy a monthly activity
which consists of socials, athletics and religious participa¬
tion. Sincere appreciations go to their capable advisor, Mrs.
M. J. Reiser, mothers’ committee consisting of Mesdames
Lil Speizer, Fred Linsey, Charles Kluglose, and Abe New¬
man, and to our sponsor Karen Speizer.

or ice skating affair. The Club’s success is due mainly to
their advisor, Mrs. Bernard Glossman, and to the mothers’
committee consisting of Mesdames Henry Bettman, Sey¬
mour Morse, Robert Gulden and Byron Morris. Special
thanks go to our CPC sponsors, Phyllis Glossman, Judy
Horovitz, Jerry Portnoy and Ross Englehardt.

===== PAGE 148 =====
Rabbis Page
One year has passed since I was deeply honored
to become the Rabbi of the Jacksonville Jewish Cen¬
ter. No year has ever passed so quickly and no year
has been so full of activities and experiences. Com¬
ing to know the program and policy of the congrega¬
tion has been a challenge and learning to know the
congregation itself has been a most gratifying experi¬
ence.
This coming year presents me with an opportu¬
nity of serving you on a much more personal and
knowledgeable basis. Our opportunities to work to¬
gether will be enhanced and mutual understanding
will become wider and deeper.
RABBI MOSHE V. GOLDBLUM
Rabbi Aronson delivering his message
at the Rabbi's Installation.
My feelings of a close personal relationship with
the Center program I hope is a contagious one. It is
so vitally necessary that we all feel that the goals of
the congregation are ours and their realization will
benefit us personally. Our personal participation and
concern will determine the success of Jewish life in
our midst.
On behalf of my wife and family, may I wish you
a very happy and healthy New Year, one of meaning¬
ful life and one of peace for all mankind.

Mr. and Mrs. Club
President Mr. and Mrs. Sidney Berkowitz
1st Vice-Pres Mr. and Mrs. Henry (Ted) Freedman
2nd Vice-Pres Mr. and Mrs. Nathan Goldstein
Treasurer Mr. and Mrs. Irving Resnick
Recording Secretary Mr. and Mrs. Barney Margolin
Corres. Secretary Mr. and Mrs. Bill Goldberg
Board Members: Messrs, and Mesdames Harold Hart, Gus
Gross, Marty Caplan, Abe Tuckman, and jack Silverman
The Mr. and Mrs. Club of Jacksonville, now in its ninth
year, provides for its membership of approximately 100 couples
a congenial and close fellowship in a year-round social atmos¬
phere. It has become one of the Jewish community’s outstand¬
ing organizations.
Each month throughout the year social functions, planned
and carried out by committees, are provided the membership.
MR. AND MRS. CLUB BOARD
These monthly affairs may vary from a family picnic to an
elaborate dinner-dance. The .annual Installation Banquet and
the New Year’s Eve Party are the highlights of each year.
Each member couple serves on at least one monthly committee.
Membership in the Club is by application, and couples
interested in affiliation are invited to contact any of the officers
or members of the Board.

♦All days of the Jewish year begin at sundown. Therefore, each holiday holiday when the Shofar (ram’s horn) sounds forth in the
really begins at sundown of the day preceding our symbol. synagogue to call the people to repentance and to rewaken re¬
sponsibility to the Lord.

PESAH (Passover), the Feast of Unleavened Bread—an eight-
day celebration of the deliveranc of the Jews from Egyptian
slavery. During the traditional Seder meal, on the first two
nights of Passover, Jewish families read the Haggadah (a ritual recita¬
tion of the story of the Exodus). Throughout the Passover periods, foods
are selected according to special dietary laws. Instead of bread, Jews
eat matzoh (unleavened bread) to recall the hasty flight from Egypt,
when there was no time to allow the bread to rise. (Hence, our matzoh
symbol.)

Camp Yarn Tov
Staff: Director, Robert Fischer, Coun¬

Staff
A new innovation with a nine-week summer Day Camping
experience within the city limits was recorded with an enroll¬
ment of 369 campers and an outstanding program. Among the
new program additions were the following:
• In addition to our midget baseball team and tadpole team
we entered a new era with a junior baseball team composed
of boys 14 through 16.
• Continued success with our bi-weekly ice skating parties at
the Jacksonville Coliseum where our Floridians enjoyed the
snow and ice.
• Our Tadpole team winning their southern Tadpole division
and finishing in the semi-finals of the city play-offs.
• Our fourth annual Color War and Award Night for the
closing highlights of another successful summer under the
direction of our Activities Director Robert Fischer.

RELIGIOUS EDUCA E/O X
Dr. Nathan Schneider, Chairman
Our school program has continued to improve.
The following innovations were introduced during
the past year:
Six Hebrew classes on Sunday morning.
Two Minyan Clubs
Expansion of special Sunday classes
Four Youth Congregations on Saturdays
Assistant counseling and teaching
Doubling the number of Ramah candidates
Foundation School for the first and second
grade
A 12th grade in the Sunday Religious School
Skill classes on Saturday mornings for special¬
ized training, Torah reading and private in¬
struction.
Principal Ted Gross
The goals in certain areas have been changed. Bas Mitzvah
will be a Friday evening affair only, Confirmation has been ad¬
vanced to the 11th grade and graduation programs will be
changed. Greater emphasis will be placed on equalized instruc¬
tion and early enrollment in the Hebrew School, as well as more
direction for all Sabbath activities.

Brandéis University, the first jewish-sponsored non-sectarian
school of higher learning, was granted a Phi Beta Kappa Char¬
ter in 1961. This came only thirteen years after the school
opened its doors on the Waltham, Massachusetts campus.
The Brandéis University National Women’s Committee,
which supports the Library at the University, played an impor¬
tant part in the Phi Beta Kappa achievement. The library pro¬
gram must keep pace with the academic program, and it is this

Officers of Brandéis University Women
Library to which the 70,000 women throughout the United
States are dedicated.
The local Brandéis University National Women’s Committee
was organized eleven years ago. No fund-raising activities are
held; all money is derived from Annual and Life Memberships
and from contributions to the Book Fund. Meetings are held
twice a year. All activities are directed to the support of the
Library, the heart of the University.

Senior Hadassah
President Mrs. Joel Fleet
President Elect Mrs. Henry D. Cristol
Vice-President Mrs. David Lewis
Vice-President Mrs. Walter Kraemer
Treasurer Mrs. Monroe Klausner
Financial Secretary Mrs. Irwin Gendzier
Recording Secretary Mrs. Edward Siegel
Corres. Secretary Mrs. Norman Moss
The Jacksonville Chapter of Hadassah was chartered by
Henrietta Szold in December 1925 and is now composed of
Senior Hadassah and the Hannah Senesch Evening Group. Its
membership is now approximately 800 and its annual quotas run
into tens of thousands.
This past season the local chapter is proud to report the ful¬
filling of all quotas. This year Hadassah sponsored, jointly with
the Jacksonville Art Association, an outstanding exhibit of
Marc Chagall’s biblical prints. On January 12 Hadassah joined
with ZOA to participate in religious services at the Center in
observance of Hadassah’s 50th anniversary. The dramatic pres¬
entation of "Woman of Valor," the biography of Henrietta
Szold, featured an Oneg Shabbat; an Education Day highlight¬
Officers of Senior Hadassah
ed Rabbi Moshe Goldblum’s review of the book "Goats of Ein
Gedi’’ and color films of Jack and Sue Becker’s recent trip to
Israel; and the Membership Tea was an outstanding event with
the announcement of the Healarama winner, Jack Becker, whose
name will be inscribed on a place on the Wall of Healing at
the new Medical Center in Israel.
The social climax of the season was reached with a spectacu¬
lar Golden Jubilee Ball in celebration of Hadassah’s half cen¬
tury of service.
Hadassah is the world’s largest Zionist organization and
has a program of health, vocational and educational service to
Israel, as well as stimulating an interest in America of the Jew¬
ish cultural heritage.
Hannah Senesch
Evening Group of Hadassah

National Council
Jacksonville Section
President Mrs. Harry Slutzah
Vice-President Mrs. Arnold Vandroff
Vice-President Mrs. Gustav Dobbie
Vice-President Mrs. Sol Goldman
Vice-President Mrs. Joel Goldman
Corres. Secretary Mrs. Benjamin Benson
Auditor Dr. Lillian Mark
Treasurer Mrs. David Gradman
Recording Secretary Mrs. L. Walter Benjamin, Jr.
Financial Secretary Mrs. Lewis Ansbacher
The National Council of Jewish Women is a volunteer
service organization which through a program of service, edu¬
cation and social action helps to meet human needs.
This past year Council sponsored Jacksonville’s first Mental
Health Fair in conjunction with the Mental Health Association
of Duval County. Because of the success enjoyed by the Fair,
Council has been asked to sponsor it again this ye,ar. Also in¬
cluded in this year’s new projects will be helping the hard-of-
hearing children under the guidance of a trained specialist in
the school system.
Council’s local projects also include recreational activities
at the Juvenile Shelter and at River Garden. In the past three
years Council has tested the hearing of almost 30,000 school
children, has continued to provide wheelchairs, crutches, and
of Jewish Women
BOARD
hospital beds through their Medical Loan Shelf and has sewed
layettes for needy families.
Council continues its support to Israel by training leaders
for welfare and educational work through scholarships and by
sending toys and clothing to children in Israel.
Through its programs and projects Council provides a
strong, unifying cord of mutual interests and aims for all
Jewish women, regardless of a diversity of thinking and back¬
ground, so that they may work together in the spirit of Judaism
for the good of all humanity.
The Jacksonville Section has both a daytime and evening
group, meeting every third Wed. and fourth Thurs., respec¬
tively.

f
Building Fund
The Priceless is Difficult to Replace
Throughout the past years Robert J. Gordon, Chairman of our Building Fund, has
given of himself with little or no consideration for his personal health or time. No sac¬
rifice was too great and no task was too difficult when it came to the Center and its
needs. Time was given by the day and not by the hour, and we all were inspired to give
and to serve through his service and devotion.
Because of ill health, Bob has not been able to continue this personal strenuous pro¬
gram of service. His spirit and guidance is difficult to equal and his outstanding price¬
less leadership is extremely difficult to replace.
May we all do our part for the Building Fund to prove to Bob that the great project
which he has nurtured in the past will continue from strength to strength in the future.
To Boh we say Hazak Vi-amatz—May you find renewed strength and vigor to con¬
tinue to inspire us for many more years.
Robert J. Gordon
Chairman

We would like to take this opportunity of extending to the
congregation, officers and lay leaders of the congregation and our
fellow staff members best wishes for a Happy and Prosperous New
Year.
BRIEF SCOPE OF ACTIVITIES
Religious Services—Traditional prayer services are held daily,
morning and evening in the Chapel.
Friday Family Services, Sabbath and Holiday Services are
observed in the Sanctuary.
As one of the outstanding Synagogue-Centers in the Southeast,
we offer to our community a unique program covering every
phase of religious, educational, social, cultural and athletic pro¬
gramming. In brief summary we are outlining our principal ac¬
tivities which are described in pictures and words throughout our
entire Year Book.
JACKSONVILLE JEWISH CENTER
" ~'~-v
Eugene Davis
Morris Montford
Willie Robinson
>—Maintenance
I
J
Annie Mae McNeil—Kitchen
Tim Riley
Wallace Mazon
Bus Drivers
Personal Religious Observances—-Traditional Jewish customs are
observed in connection with Circumcision, naming of girls,
Pidyon Ha-ben, Bar Mitzvah, Bas Mitzvah, Confirmations,
Marriages, Conversion to Judaism, Bereavement.
Education—Daily Kindergarten with outstanding program of secu¬
lar and religious content.
Hebrew School, carefully graded with intensive Hebrew con¬
tent.
Sunday School, with a curriculum including Jewish history
and customs.
Foundation School with 1st and 2nd grades of intensive secu¬
lar and Hebrew training.
Supplementary religious educational training is practiced in
Pre-Jr., Jr. Congregation, youth services and Minyan Club.
Extension Services—
Library—outstanding collection of juvenile and adult Jewish
books.
Adult Education—courses on religious and Jewish cultural
subjects.
Music—a program of religious and cultural Jewish music.
Sisterhood and Men’s Club render valuable service to the
Center and the community.
Social Activities provided by Mr. and Mrs. Club, Amity Club
and ”32 Club.”
Youth Activities
Camp Yom Tov—a nine week summer Day Camp.
Scouting—Boy Scouts, Cub Scouts, Brownies and Girl Scouts.
Athletics—programs scheduled for youth and adults.
Teen-agers are served by Center Youth League, Charles Palot
Clubs and Pre-USY, all of which are affiliated with
United Synagogue Youth. Major's Pre-Teens and Tween-
Agers serve the social needs of our younger set.

Youth Activities
Center Youth Organizations
Center Youth League—A co-ed USY Chapter for 11th and 12th graders, meeting bi¬
weekly with varied programs throughout the year.
CPC Boys—USY Chapter for 9th and 10th graders affiliated with national organization.
CPC Girls—Similar to above with a female accent on activities.
Pre-USY—Composed of 8th grade boys and girls preparing for USY membership, meet¬
ing bi-weekly.
United Synagogue Youth of which the above four clubs are members are served
by the Southeast Region Office, Rabbi Allen Rutchik, Dir., 1075 - 95th Street, Miami
Beach 54, Fla.; National Headquarters, Dr. Morton Siegel, Dir. ,1123 Broadway,
#803, New York 10, N. Y.
Boy Scouts Troop 14—For boys 11 to 14, meeting weekly on Tuesday evenings.
Cub Scouts, Pack 14—Boys 8 to 11 participate in this organization, meeting weekly at
Den Mothers’ homes with monthly Pack meetings on the last Thursday of the month.
Girl Scouts, Troop 197—For girls who have outgrown the Brownies and wish to con¬
tinue Scouting.
Brownie Troops 28, 193, 210 and 346—A Scouting organization for younger girls with
weekly gatherings.
Majors Pre-Teens Social club, monthly, for 7th grade boys and girls.
Tween-Agers—Boys and girls of the 5th and 6th grades participate in this social dub
meeting monthly.
Yom Tov
With the end of school our youth
look forward to our 9 week summer
program which is open to all chil¬
dren from 4 through 14. For the
15 year olds we offer a Counselor-
in-Training Program — with on the
job experience. This past summer
364 campers took advantage of our
summer activities.

The Tofield
Memorial Library
Committee-
Memorial Library
rasWj
Seated: Mrs. Philip Selber,
Miss Minnie Schreiber,
Mrs. Bernard Glossman
Standing: Jack Becker, Leo Meizlik
The Tofield Memorial Library, made possible by contributions
of members and friends of the Center, has as its nucleus the
personal library of our late Rabbi, Dr. Sanders A. Tofield.
Over 1500 volumes in Hebrew and English covering a wide
variety of subjects of Jewish content for adults and school
children are available for reference, study and pleasure reading.
The Library is an intergral part of the total school and syna¬
gogue program, serving the needs of students in grades Pre-
Kindergarten through Grade 12, as well as adults. The types of
material run from newspapers, magazines, film strips, records
and encyclopedia to books for information and novels.
Mr. fack Becker is Chairman of the Library Committee with
Miss Minnie Schreiber, Co-Chairman. Mrs. Byron Morris is
the representative to the Library from the Center Sisterhood.
Mrs. Philip Selber and Mrs. Bernard Glossman are the Li¬
brarians.
Committee
The Adult Education program, an integral and necessary part of the Center’s ever
broadening sphere of community improvement, has met with widespread approval and
appreciation. The weekly classes were held on Thursday evenings during the year and
were so well attended and enjoyed that they were continued through the summer. The
Rabbi, Mr. Nathan Ereidlin and Mr. Zucker conducted these classes.
In addition both the Cantor and the Rabbi led Sunday morning classes. As a further
part of the program, home study groups were formed and met periodically throughout
the season and an intensive advanced study group continued its splendid work.
It is .anticipated that the Thursday evening classes will commence again shortly after
the Holidays with some new and some repeat classes. The other study groups will con¬
tinue and new home groups will be formed.
The acceptance of this renewed effort for education is most gratifying to our lay
leadership. It is hoped that even more of our community will avail themselves of this
wonderful opportunity.
Edwin Presser
47

Jacksonville Jewish Community
President Al L. Schneider
Exec. Vice-Pres Alvin Leitman
Vice-Presidents ........ Robert H. Jacobs, I. (Scotty)
Witten, Dr. Sam Witten, Richard J. Lewinson,

Hon. Presidents Alexander Brest, P. N. Cole¬

ROBERT I. MARCUS
Serving the entire Jewish community of Jacksonville, the
Jewish Community Council is the central Welfare Fund and
Community Relations body of the local Jewish community. An
association of individuals, synagogues, organizations and social
service agencies, the program encompasses key activities which
give unity, cohesion and coordination to local Jewish communal
life.
A community-wide annual Welfare Fund Campaign pro¬
vides support to significant local, national and overseas organ¬
izations. The National United Jewish Appeal, has expressed
American Jewry’s responsibility for the welfare and rehabilita¬
tion needs of Jewish communities the world over for over 20
years. River Garden Hebrew Home for the Aged and the Jew¬
ish Welfare Society are the local beneficiaries.
The Council publishes a monthly newspaper known as the
Commentator. It is the official organ of the Council and its
member organizations.
The Council conducts a leisure time activities program which
includes Youth Council programs such as college preparation
workshops, a youth news page in the Commentator, Sunday
sports and a youth division in the annual Jewish Welfare Fund
Campaign. The Council also sponsors a community summer
Day Camp for children between the ages of 4 and 15.

SHAVUOT, 1st Day
6 SIVAN
30
Yizkor
SHAVUOT, 2nd Day
7 SIVAN
31
L.C. 7:06 p.m.
8 SIVAN
LAG BA’OMER (33rd Day of the Omer)—this holiday com¬
memorates the lifting of a plague from the students of Rabbi
Akiba, an event which occurred on the 33rd day of Count¬
ing the Omer (the counting of the “omer” or “measure” of new grain
begins on the Second Day of Passover, and continues for 49 days). In
observing Lag Ba’omer, Jews honor the memories of Rabbi Akiba and
his copatriots, Bar Kochba and Rabbi Bar Yachai. These leaders devoted
their lives to an heroic effort to end the Roman occupation and re-estab¬
lish the Jewish nation. (Rabbi Akiba ultimately died by torture at the
hands of the Romans.) The holiday is celebrated with athletic games
(symbolized here by bow and arrow) because Rabbi Akiba and his stu¬
dents carried bows and arrows to disguise their true purpose when they
went into the woods to pursue the forbidden study of the Torah.
SHAVUOT—On this day, the Ten Commandments are read in
the synagogue to commemorate the giving of the Law (Torah)
to Moses on Mount Sinai. Shavuot also marks the early wheat
harvest in the Holy Land. On this holiday Jews decorate their homes and
synagogues with greens and flowers.

===== PAGE 230 =====
Camp Ramah
Some of our Ramah campers: Leonard Selber, Howard Rosenblatt, Linda Halpern,
Simeon Goldblum, Richard Browdy, Michael Schneider ,and Mayer Gil Becker.
One of the greatest contributions that the Conservative Move¬
ment has made to American Jewish life is the program of the
Ramah camps. There are now five such camps in the United
States affecting the lives of more than 1500 of our Jewish
youth. It is indeed unfortunate when we realize that approxi¬
mately this same number is turned away each year because of
lack of space.
The program is unique in that it blends ideally the necessary
elements for ,a wholesome Jewish life. In a beautiful Jewish at¬
mosphere the Ramah camper is permitted to learn culturally,
develop spiritually, mature socially and progress athletically.
The campers and counselors are hand picked, and in this whole¬
some atmosphere a most profound impression is made upon
the youthful mind.
More campers are needed to meet the growing demand. Our
Center has benefited greatly in the opportunity granted our
young people to be a part of this program. Our Men’s Club
deserves tremendous credit for its fine Ramah scholarship
program.
The following boys and girls from Jacksonville attended
Camp Ramah in Connecticut this year: Richard Browdy, Sheila
Pages, Linda Halpern, Debbie Lederman, Leonard Selber,
Mayer Gil Becker, Simeon Goldblum, Rose Raskin, Howard
Rosenblatt, Michael Schneider.
Scene at Camp Ramah Israeli Dancing
Compliments
HENRY HODGE

Jewish Family and Children s Services
LAWRENCE RACKOW
President Lewis Meisel
Vice-Presidents Jack Coleman, Nathan Kazin,
Dr. David Konigsburg, Dr. Morris Price
Treasurer David Moss
Executive Director Lawrence Rackow
LEWIS MEISEL
To reflect the work of the Agency and to avoid the term
"welfare,” we changed our name, the fourth name change
since our organization as the United Jewish Charities in 1917.
Some find our initials JFCS easier to use. We have become
used to many variations and will answer to which form you
prefer, the long or short.
We expect by the end of the year to be in our new build¬
ing, probably in southside. We sold our building and will
have to be out by Feb. 1963. Added to our new look are our
revised by-laws which spell out specifically our current services:
Case work or counseling by a trained stafif for family groups
or individuals; child welfare to maintain Jewish children in
their own home with their own family, and if not possible to
provide foster home, institutional or residential care of Jewish
children; assistance to clients where such assistance is not other¬
wise available; .adoption; casework and admission for the River
Garden; contact with Jewish prisoners at Raiford Prison; assist¬
ance for Jewish transients; resettling Jewish immigrants in the
Jacksonville area; social welfare action, family life education
and public relations programs, training and education for social
work; research; strengthening of family functioning or stability.
Let us remind you that we are beneficiaries of the Com¬
munity Chest-United Fund and the United Jewish Welfare
Fund. Your support makes our services possible. If you can
use our services, please feel free to call us.

Zionist Organisation of America
President Henry Bettman

Iewish National Fund Max Rubin
Ex Officio ....I. M. Lieberman
Z.O.A. Board
The essential function of the Zionist Organization of Amer¬
ica is to keep alive in this country an interest in the State of
Israel. This interest is many-sided, as the efforts of Zionism
always were. The political objective was the creation of a Jewish
State. To this end it was necessary to revive the Hebrew lan¬
guage, acquire land, train colonists for settlement and raise funds
to finance the project. All this the Zionist movement did.
Today, the Z.O.A. continues to foster support for the State
of Israel. Moreover, the Z.O.A. seeks to strengthen the bonds
between American Jewry and the Jewish State on the basis of
the cultural tradition that is our common heritage.
Religious differences present no obstacle as Zionism en¬
compasses all shades of religious belief.
The Z.O.A. invites all Jewish men to join its ranks.

Gerald Sohn
This coming year promises to be a banner year for the
Center Men’s Club. Primary emphasis will be placed on en¬
couraging regular attendance at the monthly dinner meetings
on the first Thursday of every month, through a constant effort
to have interesting and informative programs, delicious meals
and attractive door prizes. The membership drive is now under
way and all interested men are encouraged to contact one of
the officers or the Center Office. Our annual paid-up member¬
ship dinner will be held on Sunday, November 4th.
In addition to providing a fine opportunity for fellowship,
the Men’s Club provides scholarships for Camp Ramah, a
Blood Bank, adult education program, sponsors Sunday Re¬
ligious School picnic, supports the Sunday morning Minyan
breakfasts, and provides awards for the Scouting program along
with scholarships to Camp Philmont.
Jr. Minyan Club Sponsored by the Men’s Club
